    • He himself will come to us tomorrow.
    • ⲁⲛϩⲉⲓ ⲉⲣⲟϥ ⲉϥⲙⲟϣⲓ ⲙⲁⲩⲁⲧϥ ⲉ ⲑⲉⲛⲉⲉⲧⲉ.
    • We found him walking by himself to the monastery.
    • ⲁ-ϩⲁⲛⲟⲩⲟⲛ ⲡⲓⲥⲧⲉⲩⲉ ⲉⲣⲟϥ, ϩⲁⲛⲕⲉⲭⲱⲟⲩⲛⲓ ⲇⲉ ⲙ̀ⲡⲟⲩⲡⲓⲥⲧⲉⲩⲉ.
    • Some believed him, but others did not believe.
    • ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲣⲉ-ⲛⲇⲓⲕⲉⲟⲥ ⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲉ ⲛⲥⲁϫⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲛⲣⲉϥⲉⲣ-ⲛⲟⲃⲓ.
    • The righteous do not listen to the words of the sinners.
    • ⲛⲉ-ϣⲁⲣⲉ-ⲙⲙⲟⲛⲁⲭⲟⲥ ϯ-ⲛⲟⲩϩⲱⲃ ⲛ̀ ϫⲓϫ ⲉⲃⲟⲗ ϧⲉⲛ ⲛⲉϩⲟⲟⲩ ⲉⲧ ⲙ̀ⲙⲁⲩ.
    • The monks used to sell their handicrafts in those days.
    • ⲛⲁⲣⲉ-ⲟⲩⲛⲓϣϯ ⲙ̀ ⲙⲏϣ ⲑⲱⲟⲩϯ ϩⲓⲣⲉⲛ ⲡⲉϥⲏⲓ.
    • A great crowd was gathered at the entrance of his house.
    • ⲙ̀ⲡⲉⲣϫⲉⲙ-ⲁⲣⲓⲕⲓ ⲉⲣⲟⲓ, ⲡⲁⲓⲱⲧ. ⲙ̀ⲡⲓⲉⲣ-ϩⲗⲓ.
    • Don't blame me, my father. I didn't do anything.
    • ⲛ̀ ⲣⲟⲩϩⲓ ⲁ-ⲡⲥⲟⲛ ⲕⲧⲟϥ ⲟⲛ ⲉ ⲧⲉϥⲣⲓ.
    • In the evening the brother returned again to his cell.
    • ⲙⲙⲟⲛ ϩⲗⲓ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲣⲟⲫⲏⲧⲏⲥ ϣⲏⲡ ϧⲉⲛ ⲡⲉϥϯⲙⲓ ⲙ̀ⲙⲓⲛ ⲙ̀ⲙⲟϥ.
    • No prophet is acceptable in his own village.
    • ⲁⲛⲟⲕ ⲇⲉ ϩⲱ ϯⲛⲁϩⲓ-ⲧⲟⲧ ⲉ ⲥϧⲁⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲛⲥⲁϫⲓ ⲉⲧⲁⲩϣⲱⲡⲓ.
    • I myself will undertake to write the things which happened.
    • ϣⲁϥϣⲁⲛϣ ⲛ̀ ⲛⲉϥϣⲏⲣⲓ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲣⲏϯ ⲛ̀ ⲟⲩⲓⲱⲧ ⲛ̀ ⲁⲅⲁⲑⲟⲥ.
    • He tends to his children like a good father.
    • ⲁϥϫⲟⲥ ⲛⲏⲓ ϫⲉ ⲑⲉⲙ-ⲣⲱⲕ ⲛ̀ⲧⲉⲕϣⲉ ⲛⲁⲕ ⲉⲃⲟⲗ.
    • He said to me, "Shut up and go away."
    • ⲁⲕⲓⲣⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲛⲁⲓ ⲛⲑⲟⲕ ⲙⲁⲩⲁⲧⲕ?
    • You (ms. sg.) alone have done these things?
    • ⲛⲓⲙ ⲡⲉⲧ ⲛⲁϣⲁⲛⲟⲩϣⲛ ⲉ-ⲁ-ⲛⲉⲛⲓⲟϯ ⲙⲟⲩ?
    • Who will rear us, our parents having died?
    • ⲁϥⲭⲁ-ⲣⲱϥ, ⲙ̀ⲡⲉϥⲟⲩⲉϣⲃ̄-ϩⲗⲓ.
    • He remained silent and answered no one / nothing.
    • ⲓⲱⲁⲛⲛⲏⲥ ⲇⲉ ϩⲱϥ ⲁϥⲙⲟⲩⲛ ⲉⲃⲟⲗ ⲉϥⲟⲩⲉϩ ϩⲓ ⲡϣⲁϥⲉ.
    • John himself continued dwelling in the desert.
    • ⲛ̄ⲧⲉⲣⲉ-ⲣⲟⲩϩⲓ ⲇⲉ ϣⲱⲡⲓ, ⲛⲉϥⲙⲁⲑⲏⲧⲏⲥ ⲁⲩⲑⲱⲟⲩϯ ϧⲉⲛ ⲡⲙⲁ ⲉⲧ ⲙ̀ⲙⲁⲩ.
    • When evening came, his disciples gathered in that place.
    • ⲛ̀ϯⲟⲩⲱϣ ⲁⲛ ⲉⲧⲣⲉⲕϭⲱ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲁⲓⲙⲁ. ⲕⲟⲧⲕ ⲉ ⲡⲉⲕⲏⲓ ⲙ̀ⲙⲓⲛ ⲙ̀ⲙⲟⲕ.
    • I do not want you (ms. sg.) to stay here. Return to your own house.
    • ⲁⲩϩⲓ-ⲧⲟⲧⲟⲩ ⲉ ⲕⲱⲧ ⲛ̀ ⲟⲩⲛⲓϣϯ ⲛ̀ ⲉⲣⲫⲉⲓ ⲉⲣⲉ-ⲧⲉϥⲁⲫⲉ ⲛⲁⲫⲟϩ ⲉ ⲧⲫⲉ ⲙⲁⲩⲁⲧⲥ.
    • They began to build a great temple whose peak (head) would reach to the sky itself.
    • ⲁ-ϣⲟⲙⲧ ⲙ̀ⲙⲱⲟⲩ ϭⲱ ⲛⲉⲙⲏⲓ, ⲛⲕⲉⲭⲱⲟⲩⲛⲓ ⲇⲉ ⲁⲩⲕⲧⲟⲟⲩ ⲉ ⲧⲃⲁⲕⲓ.
    • Three of them stayed with me, but the others returned to the city.
    • ⲛⲕⲉⲭⲱⲟⲩⲛⲓ ⲇⲉ ⲥϧⲏⲟⲩⲧ ϧⲉⲛ ⲕⲉϫⲱⲙ.
    • The other things are written in another book.
    • ⲛ̄ⲣⲉϥⲉⲣ-ⲛⲟⲃⲓ ⲇⲉ ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲩϣⲁⲛϣ-ⲛⲟⲩϣⲏⲣⲓ ϧⲉⲛ ⲛⲉⲛⲧⲟⲗⲏ ⲙ̀ ⲡϭⲟⲓⲥ.
    • The sinners do not rear their children with the commandments of the Lord.
    • ⲁⲩⲕⲟⲧⲟⲩ ⲟⲛ ⲉ ⲥⲉⲡⲥⲱⲡϥ.
    • They implored him again.
    • ⲉⲑⲃⲉ ⲟⲩ ⲧⲉⲧⲉⲛⲙⲓϣⲓ ⲛⲉⲙ ⲛⲉⲧⲉⲛⲉⲣⲏⲟⲩ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲁⲓⲣⲏϯ?
    • Why are you (pl.) quarreling with one another like this?
    • ϩⲓ ⲧⲟⲟⲩⲓ ⲇⲉ ⲁ-ⲛⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲧⲃⲁⲕⲓ ⲑⲱⲟⲩϯ ⲉ ⲧⲁⲅⲟⲣⲁ.
    • At dawn the men of the city gathered at the marketplace.
    • ⲁⲥⲉⲣ-ϩⲟϯ ⲉⲃⲟⲗ ϫⲉ ⲁ-ⲡⲉⲥϩⲁⲓ ϫⲉⲙ-ⲁⲣⲓⲕⲓ ⲉⲣⲟⲥ.
    • She was afraid, because her husband found fault with her.
    • ⲛⲓⲙ ⲡⲉϣⲁϥⲧⲁⲗϭⲉ-ⲡⲥⲏⲓⲛⲓ ⲙⲁⲩⲁⲧϥ?
    • Who heals the doctor himself?
    • ⲁⲛϩⲉⲓ ⲉ ⲛⲉⲛⲥⲛⲏⲟⲩ ⲉⲩϣⲁⲛⲉⲩϣ ⲧⲏⲣⲟⲩ ⲉ-ⲙⲙⲟⲛ ⲟⲩⲁⲓ ⲉϥϩⲟⲕⲉⲣ ⲛ̀ϧⲏⲧⲟⲩ.
    • We found our brothers all well-fed, there not being one who was hungry among them.
    • ⲧⲉⲛⲛⲁϭⲱ ⲉⲛϣⲗⲏⲗ ϣⲁ ⲣⲟⲩϩⲓ.
    • We will keep praying until evening.

Reading (from the Sayings of the Fathers)

ⲁ-ⲟⲩⲁⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲛⲉⲛⲓⲟϯ ⲧⲛ̄ⲛⲟⲟⲩ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲉϥⲙⲁⲑⲏⲧⲏⲥ ⲉ ⲙⲁϩ-ⲙⲱⲟⲩ. ⲛⲁⲣⲉ-ⲧϣⲱϯ ⲇⲉ ⲡⲉ ⲟⲩⲏⲟⲩ ⲛ̀ ⲧⲣⲓ ⲉⲙⲁϣⲱ. ⲁϥⲉⲣ-ⲡⲱⲃϣ ⲇⲉ ⲉ ϭⲓ-ⲡⲛⲟϩ ⲛⲉⲙⲁϥ. ⲛ̄ⲧⲉⲣⲉϥⲓ ⲇⲉ ⲉϫⲉⲛ ⲧϣⲱϯ, ⲁϥⲉⲙⲓ ϫⲉ ⲙ̀ⲡⲉϥⲓⲛⲓ ⲛⲉⲙⲁϥ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲛⲟϩ. ⲁϥⲓⲣⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲟⲩϣⲗⲏⲗ, ⲁϥⲙⲟⲩϯ ⲉϥϫⲱ ⲙ̀ⲙⲟⲥ ϫⲉ, "ⲡϣⲏⲓ, ⲡⲁⲓⲱⲧ ⲡⲉⲧ ϫⲱ ⲙ̀ⲙⲟⲥ ϫⲉ, 'ⲙⲟϩ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲁⲅⲅⲓⲟⲛ ⲙ̀ ⲙⲱⲟⲩ.'" ⲟⲩⲟϩ ⲛ̀ ϯⲟⲩⲛⲟⲩ ⲁ-ⲡⲙⲱⲟⲩ ⲓ ⲉⲡϣⲱⲓ, ⲁ-ⲡⲥⲟⲛ ⲙⲟϩ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲉϥϣⲟϣⲟⲩ, ⲟⲩⲟϩ ⲁ-ⲡⲙⲱⲟⲩ ϩⲉⲙⲥⲓ ⲟⲛ ⲉ ⲡⲉϥⲙⲁ.
One of our fathers sent his disciple to fetch water. But the well was very far from the cell. He forgot to bring the rope with him. And when he came upon the well, he realized that he had not brought the rope with him. He made a prayer and he called out, saying, "Oh cistern, it is my father who says to me, 'fill the bucket with water.'" And immediately, the water came upward, and the brother filled his jug, and the water settled again to its place.

New words:

  • ⲧ.ϣⲱϯ, ⲡ.ϣⲏⲓ well, cistern.
  • ⲙⲁϩ-ⲙⲱⲟⲩ to fetch water.
  • ⲡ.ⲁⲅⲅⲓⲟⲛ (τὸ ἀγγεῖον), ⲡ.ϣⲟϣⲟⲩ names of vessels.

Lesson 29

29.1 The Conditional and conditional clauses.

affirmatif négatif
1. ⲁⲓϣⲁⲛⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲁⲓϣⲧⲉⲙⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
2 m. ⲁⲕϣⲁⲛⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲁⲕϣⲧⲉⲙⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
f. ⲁⲣⲉϣⲁⲛⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲁⲣⲉϣⲧⲉⲙⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
3 m. ⲁϥϣⲁⲛⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲁϥϣⲧⲉⲙⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
f. ⲁⲥϣⲁⲛⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲁⲥϣⲧⲉⲙⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
1. ⲁⲛϣⲁⲛⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲁⲛϣⲧⲉⲙⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
2. ⲁⲣⲉⲧⲉⲛϣⲁⲛⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲁⲣⲉⲧⲉⲛϣⲧⲉⲙⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
3. ⲁⲩϣⲁⲛⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲁⲩϣⲧⲉⲙⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
Noun ⲁⲣⲉϣⲁⲛ-ⲡⲓⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲁⲣⲉϣⲧⲉⲙ-ⲡⲓⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ

The conditional clause generally precedes the main clause on which it depends.

The condition can be expressed without conjunction or by means of the conjunctions ϣⲁⲛ, ⲉϣⲱⲡ, ⲓⲥϫⲉ.

1. Without conjunction

The 3rd present and the 3rd future can sometimes express the condition by themselves:

ⲛ̀ⲑⲟⲕ ⲇⲉ ⲉⲕⲛⲁⲧⲱⲃϩ ⲙⲁϣⲉ ⲛⲁⲕ ⲉϧⲟⲩⲛ ⲉⲡⲉⲕⲧⲁⲙⲓⲟⲛ (Matthew 6:6)

but when you pray, go into your room

Most often, however, in these kinds of propositions the condition is expressed by ⲉϣⲱⲡ (391).

A very frequent conditional clause is the one formed from ⲉ- and the imperfect ⲛⲁⲣⲉ- (248) or from the auxiliary ⲛⲉ- with ⲟⲩⲟⲛ ⲙ̀ⲙⲟⲛ (302), with -ⲡⲉ, -ⲧⲉ, -ⲛⲉ (363).

It states a condition that is not supposed to be able to be fulfilled; it is rather a wish.

In the main clause which comes second, we generally use the imperfect future tense (243):

ⲉⲛⲁⲕⲭⲏ ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲓⲙⲁ ⲛⲁⲣⲉ ⲡⲁⲥⲟⲛ ⲛⲁⲙⲟⲩ ⲁⲛ ⲡⲉ (John 11:32)

If you had been here, my brother would not have died

ⲉⲛⲁⲣⲉ ⲡⲓⲛⲉⲃⲏⲓ ⲉⲙⲓ ⲛⲁϥⲛⲁⲣⲱⲓⲥ ⲡⲉ (Matthew 24:43)

If the master of the house knew, he would watch

ⲉⲛⲉ ⲟⲩⲟⲛϣϫⲟⲙ (Matthew 24:24)

if it were possible

ⲉⲛⲉ ⲫϯ ⲡⲉⲧⲉⲛⲓⲱⲧ ⲡⲉ ⲛⲁⲣⲉⲧⲉⲛⲛⲁⲙⲉⲛⲣⲓⲧ ⲡⲉ (John 8:42)

If God were your father, you would love me

ⲉⲛⲉ ⲙ̀ⲙⲟⲛ ⲛⲁⲓⲛⲁϫⲟⲥ ⲛⲱⲧⲉⲛ ⲁⲛ (John 14:2)

otherwise, I wouldn't have told you

2. With ϣⲁⲛ- (dem. ḫn)

ϣⲁⲛ- is used with the auxiliary of the 2nd present ⲁⲣⲉ- to express a future condition; it precedes the main clause.

ⲁⲕϣⲁⲛϫⲟⲥ ⲛ̀ϩⲗⲓ ⲛ̀ⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲕⲭⲏ ⲥⲁⲃⲟⲗ (Kef. 411)

if you tell anyone, you are excommunicated

ⲁⲣⲉⲧⲉⲛϣⲁⲛϯϩⲟ ⲉⲣⲟⲓ ⲁⲛⲟⲕ ⲇⲉ ⲛ̀ⲛⲁⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲉⲣⲱⲧⲉⲛ (Proverbs 1:28)

If you beg me, I will not listen to you

ⲁⲣⲉ ϣⲁⲛ ⲟⲩⲁⲓ ⲙⲟⲩⲣ ⲛ̀ⲟⲩⲭⲣⲱⲙ ϧⲉⲛ ⲕⲉⲛϥ ⲙⲏ ϥⲛⲁⲣⲱⲕϩ ⲁⲛ ⲛ̀ⲛⲓϩⲃⲱⲥ (Proverbs 6:27)

if someone ties fire to his chest, will it not burn his clothes?

In the negative clause ϣⲁⲛ- is replaced by ϣⲧⲉⲙ-:

ϯⲛⲁⲟⲩⲟⲣⲡⲕ ⲁⲛ ⲁⲕϣⲧⲉⲙ ⲥⲙⲟⲩ ⲉⲣⲟⲓ (Genesis 32:26)

I will not send you away, unless you bless me

ⲁⲣⲉϣⲧⲉⲙ ⲫϯ ϣⲱⲡⲓ ⲛⲉⲙⲁϥ (John 3:2)

if God is not with him

3. With ⲉϣⲱⲡ (Eg.* ꞽw.s ḫpr)

ⲉϣⲱⲡ used alone expresses a condition, a case that may occur, an eventuality.

It enters into the nominal clause:

ⲉϣⲱⲡ ⲉⲃⲟⲗ ϧⲉⲛ ⲛⲓⲉⲥⲱⲟⲩ ⲡⲉ ⲡⲉⲕⲇⲱⲣⲟⲛ (Leviticus 1:10)

if your offering is a sheep

It is mainly used with the 3rd present, the 3rd future, the subjunctive:

ⲉϣⲱⲡ ⲉⲩⲥⲃⲱⲕ ⲛ̀ϫⲉ ⲛⲏ ⲉⲧϧⲉⲛ ⲡⲏⲓ (Exodus 12:4)

if those in the house are not enough

ⲉϣⲱⲡ ⲉⲕⲛⲁⲓ̀ⲛⲓ ⲛ̀ⲟⲩⲇⲱⲣⲟⲛ ⲉϧⲟⲩⲛ (Leviticus 2:4)

if you present an offering

ⲉϣⲱⲡ ⲛ̀ⲧⲉ ⲡⲓⲁⲣⲭⲱⲛ ⲉⲣⲛⲟⲃⲓ (Leviticus 4:22)

if the prince comes to sin

4. With ⲉϣⲱⲡ et ϣⲁⲛ

Most often the two conjunctions are used together:

ⲉϣⲱⲡ ⲁⲕϣⲁⲛⲓⲣⲓ ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲓⲥⲁϫⲓ (Exodus 12:23)

if you do this

ⲉϣⲱⲡ ⲁⲩϣⲁⲛϯϩⲟ ⲉⲣⲟⲕ (Proverbs 1:11)

if we ask you

5. With ⲓⲥϫⲉ (Eg.* ꞽw.s r ḏd)

ⲓⲥϫⲉ, in the verbal proposition, expresses a real condition represented as already accomplished. It could be translated as "since":

ⲓⲥϫⲉ ⲁⲣⲉⲧⲉⲛⲕⲱϯ ⲛ̀ⲥⲱⲓ ⲭⲁ ⲛⲁⲓ ⲉⲃⲟⲗ ⲙⲁⲣⲟⲩϣⲉ ⲛⲱⲟⲩ (John 8:8)

if (since) it is me you seek, let these go

In the noun clause, it expresses a simple condition:

ⲓⲥϫⲉ ⲟⲩⲧⲉⲃⲛⲏ ⲡⲉ ⲓⲉ ⲟⲩⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲡⲉ (Exodus 19:13)

whether it is a beast or a man

Repeated, ⲓⲥϫⲉ separates the two members of a dilemma:

ⲓⲥϫⲉ ⲕⲁⲕⲱⲥ ⲁⲓⲥⲁϫⲓ ()

if I spoke badly, gives proof of evil

ⲓⲥϫⲉ ⲇⲉ ⲕⲁⲗⲱⲥ (John 18:23)

but if I spoke well, why are you hitting me?

"If not" translates as ⲓⲥϫⲉ ⲙ̀ⲙⲟⲛ, sometimes as ⲉϣⲱⲡ ⲙ̀ⲙⲟⲛ, rarely as ⲙ̀ⲙⲟⲛ alone.

Negation is with -ϣⲧⲉⲙ-: ⲁϥϣⲁⲛϣⲧⲉⲙⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ, ⲁⲣϣⲁⲛϣⲧⲉⲙ-ⲡⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ. ϣⲁⲛ may be omitted in the negative: ⲁϥϣⲧⲉⲙⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ, ⲁⲣⲉϣⲧⲉⲙ-ⲡⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ. The Conditional occurs only in the protasis of conditional sentences. Only the Infinitive may occur in the verbal slot.

Conditional sentences in Coptic fall formally into two clearly defined groups: (1) real, and (2) contrary-to-fact. The protasis of real conditional sentences in present time has a variety of forms:

  1. a clause with the Conditional:

    ⲁⲕϣⲁⲛⲡⲓⲥⲧⲉⲩⲉ ⲉ ⲛⲁⲓ
    if you believe this

  2. ⲉϣⲱⲡ (if) or ⲓⲥϫⲉ (if) followed by the First Present, the Circumstantial, the Conditional, or any type of nonverbal predication:

    ⲉϣⲱⲡ/ⲓⲥϫⲉ ⲕⲡⲓⲥⲧⲉⲩⲉ ⲉ ⲛⲁⲓ
    " ⲉⲕⲡⲓⲥⲧⲉⲩⲉ ⲉ ⲛⲁⲓ
    " ⲁⲕϣⲁⲛⲡⲓⲥⲧⲉⲩⲉ ⲉ ⲛⲁⲓ
    if you believe this
    " ⲛⲑⲟⲕ ⲡⲉ ⲡⲉϥⲓⲱⲧ
    if you are his father
    " ⲟⲩⲟⲛⲧⲁⲕ ⲡϩⲁⲧ
    if you have the money
    " ⲛ̀ϯⲙⲡϣⲁ ⲁⲛ
    if I am not worthy

  3. the Circumstantial alone often serves as protasis:

    ⲉⲛⲙ̀ ⲡⲁⲓⲙⲁ, …
    since we are here, …

The apodosis of such conditions may be any variety of verbal clause appropriate for the required sense (e.g. Fut. I, II, III; Habitual; Imperative). The apodosis may optionally be introduced with ⲓⲉ (ⲉⲉⲓⲉ). For examples, see the exercises.

The protasis of contrary-to-fact conditions is in fact an Imperfect circumstantial clause, or, in the case of nonverbal clauses, a circumstantial of the clause with the imperfect converter:

ⲉ-ⲛⲁϥⲟⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲟⲩⲣⲟ if he were king
ⲉ-ⲛⲉ-ⲛⲑⲟϥ ⲡⲉ ⲡⲟⲩⲣⲟ if he were the king
ⲉ-ⲛⲉ-ⲟⲩⲟⲛⲧⲁⲛ ⲟⲩⲟⲩⲣⲟ if we had a king
ⲉ-ⲛⲉⲧⲉⲧⲉⲛⲙ̀ ⲡⲁⲓⲙⲁ if you were here

In past time ⲉ-ⲛⲉ- is followed by the affirmative Second Perfect or negative First Perfect:

ⲉ-ⲛⲉ-ⲛⲧⲁⲕϯ-ⲡϩⲁⲧ ⲛⲁⲓ
if you had given me the money
ⲉ-ⲛⲉ-ⲙ̀ⲡⲉⲕϭⲓ-ⲡϩⲁⲧ
if you had not taken the money

If the clause is nonverbal, ⲉ-ⲛⲉ- alone is used. Thus, ⲉ-ⲛⲁⲕⲙ̀ ⲡⲁⲓⲙⲁ means both "if you were here" and "if you had been here".

The conditional prefix ⲉ-ⲛⲉ- is not to be confused with the particle ⲁⲛ which serves to introduce a question, e.g. ⲁⲛ ⲁⲕⲛⲁⲩ ⲉⲣⲟϥ? Did you see him?

The apodosis of both tenses is in the imperfect of the Future:

ⲉ-ⲛⲁⲕⲡⲓⲥⲧⲉⲩⲉ, ⲛⲁⲣⲉ-ⲫⲁⲓ ⲛⲁϣⲱⲡⲓ ⲁⲛ.
If you believed, this would not happen.
ⲉ-ⲛⲉ-ⲛⲧⲁⲕⲡⲓⲥⲧⲉⲩⲉ, ⲛⲁⲣⲉ-ⲫⲁⲓ ⲛⲁϣⲱⲡⲓ ⲁⲛ.
If you had believed, this would not have hapened.

The Greek conjunctions ⲉⲓⲙⲏⲧⲓ (εἰ μή τι) and ⲕⲁⲛ (κἄν) are also used to introduce protases of both real and contrary-to-fact conditions.

ⲛ̀ⲥⲁⲃⲏⲗ ϫⲉ (except that, unless, if not) is often used to introduce the protasis of a contrary-to-fact condition; the clause usually contains a Pres. I, Perf. I, or nonverbal predication:

ⲛ̀ⲥⲁⲃⲏⲗ ϫⲉ ⲕⲡⲓⲥⲧⲉⲩⲉ if you did not believe
" ⲁⲕⲡⲓⲥⲧⲉⲩⲉ if you had not believed
" ⲛⲑⲟⲕ ⲡⲉ ⲡⲁⲓⲱⲧ if you were not my father

29.2 Inflected predicate adjectives. There is a small set of predicate adjectives inflected by means of pronominal suffixes or by proclisis to a nominal subject, e.g.

ⲛⲉⲥⲉ-ⲧⲉϥⲥϩⲓⲙⲓ. His wife is beautiful.
ⲛⲉⲥⲱⲥ. She is beautiful.

The more important of these are ⲛⲁⲁ- ⲛⲁⲁ⸗ great, ⲛⲁⲛⲉ- ⲛⲁⲛⲉ⸗ good, ⲛⲉⲥⲉ- ⲛⲉⲥⲱ⸗ beautiful, ⲛⲉⲥⲃⲱⲱ⸗ wise, ⲛⲁϣⲉ- ⲛⲁϣⲱ⸗ numerous, ⲛⲉϭⲱ⸗ ugly. When used in relative clauses, they are treated like the First Present: ⲡⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲉⲧ ⲛⲁⲛⲉϥ the good man, ⲡⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲉⲧⲉ ⲛⲉⲥⲉ-ⲧⲉϥⲥϩⲓⲙⲓ the man whose wife is beautiful. They may also be preceded by the imperfect and circumstantial converters: ⲛⲉ-ⲛⲁⲛⲉϥ (ⲡⲉ) he was good; ⲟⲩⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲉ-ⲛⲁⲛⲉϥ (ⲡⲉ) a good man. ⲛⲁⲓⲁⲧ⸗ (blessed is/are) belongs to this group, but a following nominal subject must be anticipated with a suffix: ⲛⲁⲓⲁⲧⲟⲩ ⲛ̀ ⲛⲣⲉϥⲉⲣ-ⲉⲓⲣⲏⲛⲏ blessed are the peacemakers.

29.3 The comparison of both attributive and predicate adjectives is expressed by placing the preposition ⲉ before the item on which the comparison is based: ⲛⲓϣϯ ⲉ ⲫⲁⲓ greater than this, ⲥⲁⲃⲉ ⲉ ⲛⲉϥⲥⲛⲏⲟⲩ wiser than his brothers. In addition to simple adjectives, both Coptic and Greek, the predicate adjectives of the preceding paragraph as well as appropriate qualitatives and other verbal constructions may be used in this construction. E.g.

ⲛⲁϥⲟⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲛⲓϣϯ ⲉ ⲛⲉϥⲥⲛⲏⲟⲩ.
He was more important than his brothers.
ϥϭⲟⲥⲓ ⲉ ⲡⲉϥϭⲟⲓⲥ.
He is more exalted than his master.
ⲛⲁϥⲟⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲟⲩⲱⲓⲛⲓ ⲉ ⲡⲣⲏ.
It was brighter than the sun.
ⲛⲉⲥⲱⲥ ⲉ ⲧⲉⲥⲥⲱⲛⲓ.
She is more beautiful than her sister.

A comparison may be strengthened by using ϩⲟⲩⲟ (more) in various combinations: ⲛ̀ ϩⲟⲩⲟ ⲉ, ⲉ ϩⲟⲩⲟ ⲉ, ⲉ ϩⲟⲩⲉ, all meaning "more than". ⲛ̀ ϩⲟⲩⲟ alone may express an absolute comparative: ⲡⲛⲓϣϯ ⲛ̀ ϩⲟⲩⲟ the greater.

The Greek preposition ⲡⲁⲣⲁ (or ⲙ̀ ⲡⲁⲣⲁ) may be used instead of ⲉ. Suffixes may be attached: ⲡⲁⲣⲟⲓ, ⲡⲁⲣⲟⲕ, ⲡⲁⲣⲟ etc.

29.4 Nouns with possessive suffixes (continued).

  1. ⲣⲁⲧ⸗ (foot) was mentioned in §19.2 in connection with ⲉⲣⲁⲧ⸗ and ⲟϩⲓ ⲉⲣⲁⲧ⸗. Other compounds include ϧⲁ ⲣⲁⲧ⸗ prep. under, at the foot of; ⲭⲁ-ⲣⲁⲧ⸗ to set foot (+ ⲉⲃⲟⲗ: to start out); ⲙⲟϣⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲣⲁⲧ⸗ to go on foot.
  2. ϩⲣⲁ⸗ is the presuffixal form of two words: (1) ϩⲟ ϩⲣⲁ⸗ face; (2) ϧⲣⲱⲟⲩ ϧⲁⲣⲁ⸗ voice. Both of these words are common in their unbound forms. Compounds worth noting are ⲉϩⲣⲉⲛ ⲉϩⲣⲁ⸗ prep. toward (the face of); (ⲛ̀) ⲛⲁϩⲣⲉⲛ (ⲛ̄) ⲛⲁϩⲣⲁ⸗ prep. in the presence of; ϭⲓ-ϩⲣⲁ⸗ (Q ϭⲓ-ϩⲣⲁⲉⲓⲧ) to amuse oneself, be diverted, distracted (suff. is reflex.); ϥⲓ-ϩⲣⲁ⸗ to raise one's voice, utter (± ⲉⲃⲟⲗ, ⲉϩⲣⲏⲓ).
  3. ϩⲑⲏ⸗ is the presuffixal form of (1) ϩⲏⲧ heart, mind, and (2) ϩⲏⲧ tip, edge. Compounds using the form include ϯ-ϩⲑⲏ⸗ to observe, pay attention to (ⲉ, ⲉϫⲉⲛ); ϣⲁⲛ-ϩⲑⲏ⸗ to have pity (on: ⲉϫⲉⲛ, ⲉϩⲣⲏⲓ ⲉϫⲉⲛ); and the prep. ϩⲁϩⲧⲉⲛ ϩⲁϩⲧⲏ⸗.
  4. ϩⲏⲧ⸗ is the presuffixal form of (1) ⲧ.ϩⲏ belly, womb, and (2) ⲧ.ϩⲏ front. ϧⲏⲧ⸗ (belly, womb) may be used in its plain sense, as in ϧⲉⲛ ϧⲏⲧⲥ̄ in her womb; otherwise it appears only as part of the prep. ϧⲉⲛ ⲛ̀ϧⲏⲧ⸗. ϩⲏⲧ⸗ (front) is used as a preposition with certain verbs, e.g. ϣⲓⲡⲓ ϩⲏⲧ⸗, ⲉⲣ-ϩⲟϯ ϩⲏⲧ⸗.
  5. ⲑⲟⲩⲱ⸗ (bosom) is found in the prepositions ⲉⲧⲟⲩⲛ̄- ⲉⲧⲟⲩⲱ⸗ and ϩⲓⲧⲟⲩⲛ̄- ϩⲓⲑⲟⲩⲱ⸗ near, beside. The latter is frequent in the relative construction ⲡⲉⲧ ϩⲓⲑⲟⲩⲱ⸗ neighbor, e.g. ⲡⲉⲧ ϩⲓⲑⲟⲩⲱϥ his neighbor.

Other nouns used with pronominal suffixes are ⲁⲩⲣⲏϫ⸗ end, ⲕⲉⲛ(ⲧ)⸗ bosom, ⲣⲉⲛ(ⲧ)⸗ name, ⲥⲟⲩⲉⲛ⸗ price, and ϣⲁⲛⲧ⸗ nose. The Glossary may be consulted for these.

Vocabulary 29

(ⲉϣⲱⲡ, ⲓⲥϫⲉ, ⲛ̀ⲥⲁⲃⲏⲗ ϫⲉ, ⲛⲁⲛⲉ-, ⲛⲉⲥⲉ-, ⲛⲁϣⲉ-, ⲛⲁⲓⲁⲧ⸗, ⲛ̀ ϩⲟⲩⲟ ⲉ, ϥⲓ-ϩⲣⲁ⸗, ϣⲁⲛ-ϩⲑⲏ⸗ ⲉϫⲉⲛ, ⲡⲉⲧ ϩⲓⲑⲟⲩⲱ⸗ from the lesson)

  • ⲱⲥⲕ, Q ⲟⲥⲕ vb. intr. to delay, tarry; to be prolonged, continue; + Circum.: to continue (doing).
  • ⲥⲱϩⲓ ⲥⲁϩⲉ- ⲥⲁϩⲱ⸗ Q ⲥⲁϩⲏⲟⲩⲧ vb. reflex. + ⲉⲃⲟⲗ to withdraw, leave (from: ⲙ̀ⲙⲟ⸗).
  • ⲑⲁⲙⲓⲟ ⲑⲁⲙⲓⲉ- ⲑⲁⲙⲓⲟ⸗ Q ⲑⲁⲙⲓⲏⲟⲩⲧ vb. tr. to create, make; to prepare, make ready (ⲙ̀ⲙⲟ⸗); as n.m. creation, creature.
  • ⲑⲉⲃⲓⲟ ⲑⲃ̄ⲃⲓⲉ- ⲑⲉⲃⲓⲟ⸗ Q ⲑⲉⲃⲓⲏⲟⲩⲧ vb. tr. to humble, humiliate; intr. and reflex. to become humble; as n.m. humility (often + ⲛ̀ ϩⲏⲧ).
  • ⲡ.ϩⲙⲟⲧ grace, gift, favor; gratitude. ϣⲉⲡ-ϩⲙⲟⲧ ⲛ̀ⲧⲉⲛ to give thanks to (for: ⲉϫⲉⲛ, ϩⲓ, ϧⲁ); ϫⲉⲙ-ϩⲙⲟⲧ to find favor.
  • ϣⲟⲣⲡ (f. ϣⲟⲣⲡⲓ) adj. first, before or after n. with ⲛ̀. ⲛ̀ ϣⲟⲣⲡ adv. formerly, at first.
  • ⲉⲣ-ϩⲟⲩⲟ ⲉ (Q ⲟⲓ ⲛ̀) to exceed, be more than; to be in excess, more than enough for.
  • ϧⲉⲛ ⲟⲩⲱⲣϫ adv. firmly, surely, certainly, diligently.

Exercises

      • ⲉⲑⲃⲉ ⲡⲉⲕⲑⲉⲃⲓⲟ ⲛ̀ ϩⲏⲧ ϥⲛⲁϣⲁⲛ-ϩⲑⲏϥ ⲉϫⲱⲕ.
      • Because of your (ms. sg.) humility of heart, he will have pity on you.
      • ⲛⲓⲙ ⲡⲉⲧⲁϥⲑⲁⲙⲓⲟ ⲙ̀ ⲡϣⲟⲣⲡ ⲛ̀ ⲣⲱⲙⲓ?
      • Who created the first man?
      • ⲛⲁϣⲉ-ⲛⲁⲓⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲛ̀ ϩⲟⲩⲟ ⲉⲣⲟⲛ.
      • These men are more numerous than us.
      • ⲛⲉⲥⲉ-ⲧⲁⲓⲃⲁⲕⲓ ⲛ̀ ϩⲟⲩⲟ.
      • This city is the more beautiful.
      • ⲛⲁⲓⲁⲧⲟⲩ ⲛ̀ ⲛϩⲏⲕⲓ.
      • Blessed are the poor.
      • ⲁ-ⲫⲛⲟⲩϯ ⲑⲁⲙⲓⲉ-ⲧⲫⲉ ⲛⲉⲙ ⲡⲕⲁϩⲓ.
      • God created heaven and the earth.
      • ⲛⲓⲙ ⲡⲉ ⲡⲉⲧ ϩⲓⲑⲟⲩⲱⲕ?
      • Who is your (ms. sg.) neighbor?
      • ⲑⲁⲓ ⲧⲉ ⲧϣⲟⲣⲡⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲉⲛⲧⲟⲗⲏ.
      • This is the first commandment.
      • ⲛⲁⲛⲉ-ϯ-ⲙⲏϣ ⲙ̀ ⲙⲉⲧⲁⲛⲟⲓⲁ.
      • It is good to repent much.
      • ⲥⲉⲛⲁⲥⲙⲟⲩ ⲉⲣⲟⲕ ⲛ̀ ϩⲟⲩⲟ ⲉ ⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲛⲓⲃⲉⲛ.
      • You (ms. sg.) will be blessed more than any man.
      • ⲛⲉⲩⲟⲛⲧⲁϥ ⲟⲩⲥϩⲓⲙⲓ ⲉ-ⲛⲉⲥⲱⲥ ⲉⲙⲁϣⲱ.
      • He had a very beautiful wife.
      • ⲁⲥⲑⲁⲙⲓⲟ ⲛⲁϥ ⲛ̀ ⲟⲩⲕⲟⲩϫⲓ ⲛ̀ ϫⲓⲛⲟⲩⲱⲙ.
      • She prepared him a little food.
      • ⲛⲁⲓⲁⲧϥ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲉⲧⲁϥϫⲉⲙ-ϩⲙⲟⲧ ⲛ̀ⲛⲁϩⲣⲉⲛ ⲡϭⲟⲓⲥ.
      • Blessed is the one who has found favor in the presence of the Lord.
      • ⲟⲩ ⲡⲉⲧ ⲛⲁϣⲑⲉⲃⲓⲟⲕ?
      • What can humble you (ms. sg.)?
      • ⲟⲩ ⲡⲉⲧⲉⲛⲛⲁⲁⲁϥ ϫⲉ ⲉⲛⲉⲟⲩϫⲁⲓ?
      • What will we do to be saved?
      • ⲥⲁϩⲉ-ⲑⲏⲛⲟⲩ ⲉⲃⲟⲗ ⲙ̀ⲙⲟⲓ.
      • Leave (pl.) me.
      • ⲁϥϣⲁⲛϫⲉⲙⲧ, ϥⲛⲁⲙⲱⲟⲩⲧ ⲙ̀ⲙⲟⲓ.
      • If he finds me he will kill me.
      • ⲁⲕϣⲁⲛⲥⲟⲧⲡⲧ, ⲓⲉ ⲛⲁⲥⲛⲏⲟⲩ ⲛⲁϫⲱⲛⲧ ⲉⲙⲁϣⲱ.
      • If you (ms. sg.) choose me, then my brothers will become very angry.
      • ⲁⲕϣⲁⲛⲭⲁⲧ ⲉ ϣⲉ ⲛⲏⲓ, ϯⲛⲁⲕⲧⲟⲓ ⲉ ϣⲓⲏⲧ.
      • If you (ms. sg.) let me go, I will return to Scetis.
      • ⲁϥϣⲁⲛϩⲱⲛ ⲉⲧⲟⲧⲕ ⲉⲧⲣⲉⲭⲁⲥ, ⲉⲕⲉⲁⲓⲥ ϧⲉⲛ ⲟⲩⲱⲣϫ̄.
      • If he commands you (ms. sg.) to do it, you must do it diligently.
      • ⲉϣⲱⲡ ⲙⲙⲁⲧⲟⲓ ⲓ ⲉϧⲟⲩⲛ ⲉ ⲧⲃⲁⲕⲓ, ⲥⲉⲛⲁⲣⲁϧⲧⲛ ⲧⲏⲣⲛ.
      • If the soldiers come in to the city, they will kill us all.
      • ⲉϣⲱⲡ ϥⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲉ ⲧⲉⲕⲥⲙⲏ, ϥⲛⲁⲥⲁϩⲱϥ.
      • If he hears your (ms. sg.) voice, he will leave.
      • ⲉϣⲱⲡ ⲟⲩⲟⲛⲧⲏⲧⲉⲛ ϩⲁⲛⲱⲓⲕ ⲙ̀ⲙⲁⲩ ⲉⲩⲉⲣ-ϩⲟⲩⲟ ⲉⲣⲱⲧⲉⲛ, ⲧⲉⲧⲛⲉⲧⲏⲓⲧⲟⲩ ⲛ̀ ⲛⲉⲧ ϩⲟⲕⲉⲣ.
      • If you (pl.) have more than enough bread for yourselves, you shall give it to the hungry.
      • ⲁⲣϣⲁⲛ-ⲛⲥⲛⲏⲟⲩ ⲕⲧⲟⲟⲩ ⲉ ⲡϯⲙⲓ ϩⲓ ⲣⲟⲩϩⲓ, ϯⲛⲁϣⲉ ⲛⲏⲓ ⲛⲉⲙⲱⲟⲩ.
      • If the brothers return to the village in the evening, I will go with them.
      • ⲓⲥϫⲉ ⲡⲉⲕⲓⲱⲧ ⲉⲡⲓⲧⲓⲙⲁ ⲛⲁⲕ, ⲛ̀ⲛⲉⲕϫⲱⲛⲧ.
      • If your (ms. sg.) father rebukes you, you shall not become angry.
      • ⲓⲥϫⲉ ⲡⲉⲕⲥⲟⲛ ⲉⲣ-ⲡⲉⲧϩⲱⲟⲩ ⲛⲁⲕ, ⲉⲕⲉⲉⲣ-ⲡⲡⲉⲧ ⲛⲁⲛⲉϥ ⲛⲁϥ.
      • If your (ms. sg.) brother does evil to you, you shall do good to him.
      • ⲁⲣϣⲁⲛ-ⲧⲉⲕⲥⲱⲛⲓ ⲓ ϣⲁⲣⲟⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲣⲁⲥϯ, ϯⲛⲁⲧⲁⲙⲟⲥ ⲉⲑⲃⲉ ⲡⲁⲓⲥⲁϫⲓ.
      • If your (ms. sg.) sister comes to me tomorrow, I will tell her about this thing.
      • ⲉ-ⲛⲉ-ⲟⲩⲇⲓⲕⲉⲟⲥ ⲡⲉ ⲛⲑⲟⲕ, ⲛⲁⲕⲛⲁⲓⲣⲓ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲁⲓⲣⲏϯ ⲁⲛ.
      • If you (ms. sg.) were righteous, you would not act like this.
      • ⲁⲣⲉϫⲉⲙ-ϩⲙⲟⲧ ⲛ̀ⲛⲁϩⲣⲉⲛ ⲫⲛⲟⲩϯ.
      • You (fm. sg.) have found favor before God.
      • ⲉ-ⲛⲁⲕⲙ̀ ⲡⲁⲓⲙⲁ, ⲛⲁⲣⲉ-ⲡⲁⲥⲟⲛ ⲛⲁⲙⲟⲩ ⲁⲛ ⲡⲉ.
      • If you (ms. sg.) had been here, my brother would not have died.
      • ⲧⲉⲛϣⲉⲡ-ϩⲙⲟⲧ ⲛ̀ⲧⲟⲧⲕ ϧⲁ ⲡⲉⲕⲛⲓϣϯ ⲛ̀ ⲛⲁⲓ.
      • We give you (ms. sg.) thanks for your great mercy.
      • ⲉ-ⲛⲉ-ⲛⲧⲁⲓⲉⲙⲓ ϫⲉ ⲛⲑⲟⲕ ⲡⲉ ⲡⲟⲩⲣⲟ, ⲛⲁⲓⲛⲁⲫⲁϧⲧ ⲛⲁϩⲣⲁⲕ ⲡⲉ ⲉⲓϣⲓⲡⲓ ϩⲏⲧⲕ.
      • If I had understood that you (ms. sg.) were the king, I would have bowed in your presence, revering you.
      • ⲓⲥϫⲉ ⲕⲱⲥⲕ ⲉⲕⲟⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲣⲉϥⲉⲣ-ⲛⲟⲃⲓ, ⲛ̀ⲧⲟⲩⲛⲁϣⲁⲛ-ϩⲑⲏⲟⲩ ⲉϫⲱⲕ ⲁⲛ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲉϩⲟⲟⲩ ⲉⲧ ⲙ̀ⲙⲁⲩ.
      • If you (ms. sg.) continue being sinful, you will not be pitied on that day.
      • ⲉϣⲱⲡ ⲥⲉⲓⲣⲓ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲉⲧ ⲛⲁⲛⲉϥ, ⲥⲉⲛⲁϫⲉⲙ-ϩⲙⲟⲧ ⲛ̄ⲛⲁϩⲣⲙ̄ ⲡϫⲟⲉⲓⲥ.
      • If they do good, they will find favor in the presence of the Lord.
      • ⲉ-ⲛⲉ-ⲛⲧⲁ-ⲛⲁⲓϧⲓⲥⲓ ⲱⲥⲕ, ⲛⲁⲛⲛⲁⲙⲟⲩ ⲡⲉ.
      • If these afflictions had been prolonged, we would have died.
      • ⲉϣⲱⲡ ⲉⲩⲡⲓⲥⲧⲉⲩⲉ ϧⲉⲛ ⲟⲩⲱⲣϫ, ⲥⲉⲛⲁⲥⲉⲗⲥⲱⲗⲟⲩ.
      • If they firmly believe, they will be consoled.
      • ⲥϣⲉ ⲉⲣⲟⲛ ⲉⲧⲣⲉⲛϣⲉⲡ-ϩⲙⲟⲧ ⲛ̀ⲧⲟⲧϥ ⲛ̀ ⲥⲏⲟⲩ ⲛⲓⲃⲉⲛ.
      • It is proper for us to thank him always.
      • ϩⲱϯ ⲉⲣⲟⲛ ⲉⲧⲣⲉⲛϯ-ⲧⲟⲧⲟⲩ ⲛ̀ ⲛⲉⲧ ϩⲓⲑⲟⲩⲱⲛ.
      • It is necessary for us to help our neighbors.
      • ⲥⲙⲟⲕϩ ⲉ ⲥϧⲁⲓ ⲙ̀ ⲙⲉⲧⲣⲉⲙⲛ̀ⲭⲏⲙⲓ.
      • It is difficult to write Coptic / Egyptian!
      • ⲓⲥ ⲡⲁⲓⲛⲓϣϯ ⲙ̀ ⲙⲏⲓⲛⲓ ⲛⲁϭⲱⲣⲡ ⲉⲃⲟⲗ ⲛⲱⲧⲉⲛ.
      • Behold, this great sign will appear to you.
      • ⲛ̀ⲥⲁⲃⲏⲗ ϫⲉ ⲛⲑⲟⲕ ⲡⲉ ⲡⲁⲓⲱⲧ, ⲛⲁⲓⲛⲁⲙⲟⲟⲩⲧⲕ̄.
      • If you (ms. sg.) were not my father, I would kill you.

Reading
(from the Sayings of the Fathers)

    • ⲁϥϫⲟⲥ ⲛ̀ϫⲉ ⲟⲩϧⲉⲗⲗⲟ ϫⲉ "ϧⲉⲛ ⲡⲓⲣⲁⲥⲙⲟⲥ ⲛⲓⲃⲉⲛ ⲙ̀ⲡⲉⲣϫⲉⲙ-ⲁⲣⲓⲕⲓ ⲉ-ⲣⲱⲙⲓ, ⲁⲗⲗⲁ ϫⲉⲙ-ⲁⲣⲓⲕⲓ ⲉⲣⲟⲕ ⲙⲁⲩⲁⲧⲕ ⲉⲕϫⲱ ⲙ̀ⲙⲟⲥ ϫⲉ 'ⲉⲣⲉ-ⲛⲁⲓ ϣⲟⲡ ⲙ̀ⲙⲟⲓ ⲉⲑⲃⲉ ⲛⲁⲛⲟⲃⲓ'."
    • A monk said, "In every temptation, don't find fault with man, but find fault with yourself alone, saying, 'It is because of my sins that these things are happening to me.'"
    • ⲁ-ⲟⲩⲁⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲛϧⲉⲗⲗⲟ ϣⲉ ⲛⲁϥ ϣⲁ ⲕⲉϧⲉⲗⲗⲟ ⲟⲩⲟϩ ⲡⲉϫⲁϥ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲉϥⲙⲁⲑⲏⲧⲏⲥ ϫⲉ, "ⲑⲁⲙⲓⲟ ⲛⲁⲛ ⲛ̀ ⲟⲩⲕⲟⲩϫⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲁⲣϣⲓⲛ". ⲟⲩⲟϩ ⲁϥⲑⲁⲙⲓⲟϥ. ⲡⲉϫⲁϥ ϫⲉ, "ϩⲉⲣⲡ̄-ϩⲁⲛⲱⲓⲕ ⲛⲁⲛ". ⲟⲩⲟϩ ⲁϥϩⲟⲣⲡⲟⲩ. ⲛⲑⲱⲟⲩ ⲇⲉ ⲁⲩⲙⲟⲩⲛ ⲉⲃⲟⲗ ⲉⲩⲥⲁϫⲓ ⲉ ⲛⲡ︤ⲛ︦ⲓ︥ⲕⲟⲛ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲉϩⲟⲟⲩ ⲧⲏⲣϥ ⲛⲉⲙ ⲡⲉϫⲱⲣϩ ⲧⲏⲣϥ.
    • One of the monks went up to another monk and said to his disciple, "Prepare us a few lentils." And he prepared it. He said, "Moisten some loaves for us." And he moistened them. And they kept speaking of spiritual matters all day and all night.
    • ⲁⲩϫⲟⲥ ⲛ̀ϫⲉ ⲛϧⲉⲗⲗⲟ ϫⲉ, "ⲕⲁⲛ ⲛⲁⲙⲉ ⲁⲣϣⲁⲛ-ⲟⲩⲁⲅⲅⲉⲗⲟⲥ ⲟⲩⲱⲛϩ ⲛⲁⲕ ⲉⲃⲟⲗ, ⲙ̀ⲡⲉⲣϣⲟⲡϥ ⲉⲣⲟⲕ, ⲁⲗⲗⲁ ⲑⲉⲃⲓⲟⲕ ⲛ̀ⲧⲉⲕϫⲟⲥ ϫⲉ, 'ⲛ̀ϯⲙⲡϣⲁ ⲁⲛ ⲉ ⲛⲁⲩ ⲉ ⲡⲁⲅⲅⲉⲗⲟⲥ ⲉ-ⲁⲓⲱⲛϧ ϧⲉⲛ ⲛⲛⲟⲃⲓ'."
    • The monks said, "Even if an angel truly appears to you, do not receive it (to yourself), but humble yourself and say, 'I am not worthy to see the angel, having lived in sins."

New words:

  • ⲡ.ⲡⲓⲣⲁⲥⲙⲟⲥ (ὁ πειρασμός) temptation.
  • ⲡ.ⲁⲣϣⲓⲛ lentils.
  • ϩⲱⲣⲡ ϩⲉⲣⲡ̄- ϩⲟⲣⲡ⸗ vb. tr. to moisten.
  • ⲡ︤ⲛ︦ⲓ︥ⲕⲟⲛ = ⲡⲛⲉⲩⲙⲁⲧⲓⲕⲟⲛ spiritual matter(s).

Lesson 30

30.1 The Injunctive (also called the Optative):

ⲙⲁⲣⲓⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ let me hear ⲙⲁⲣⲉⲛⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ let us hear
ⲙⲁⲣⲉϥⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ let him hear ⲙⲁⲣⲟⲩⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ let them hear
ⲙⲁⲣⲉⲥⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ let her hear
ⲙⲁⲣⲉ-ⲡⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ let the man hear

The Injunctive occurs only in the 1st and 3rd persons in standard Sahidic. The 1st person corresponds to the cohortative, the 3rd person to the jussive; theoretically, the Imperative may be said to occupy the 2nd person position. The negative of the Injunctive is expressed by using the negative Imperative prefix ⲙ̀ⲡⲉⲣ- with the corresponding form of the Inflected Infinitive: ⲙ̀ⲡⲉⲣⲧⲣⲉϥϣⲉ ⲛⲁϥ don't let him go, ⲙ̀ⲡⲉⲣⲧⲣⲉⲩⲙⲟⲟⲩⲧϥ̄ don't let them kill him. The Injunctive is tripartite and is used only with the Infinitive. The free form of the 1st person, ⲙⲁⲣⲟⲛ, is used alone in the sense "Let's go."

30.2 The Future Conjunctive of Result (also called the Finalis).

— ⲧⲁⲣⲛ̄ⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲧⲁⲣⲉ-ⲡⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
ⲧⲁⲣⲉⲕⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲧⲁⲣⲉⲧⲛ̄ⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
ⲧⲁⲣⲉⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
ⲧⲁⲣⲉϥⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲧⲁⲣⲟⲩⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
ⲧⲁⲣⲉⲥⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ

ⲛ̀ may occur optionally before all of these forms. For the 1st person sing. the simple Conjunctive ⲧⲁ- may be used.

The Future Conjunctive is basically a result clause; it is especially frequent after an Imperative, e.g.

ⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲉⲣⲟⲓ ⲧⲁⲣⲉⲕⲉⲣ-ⲥⲁⲃⲉ. Listen to me and you will become wise (or: so as to become wise).

Although the Conjunctive itself may occasionally have the value of a result/purpose clause after an Imperative, the Future Conjunctive always has this meaning. The nuance of the form can best be understood if it is viewed as the transformation of an underlying conditional sentence:

ⲁⲙⲟⲩ ⲧⲁⲣⲉⲕⲛⲁⲩ. ← ⲁⲕϣⲁⲛⲓ ⲓⲉ ⲕⲛⲁⲛⲁⲩ.

It may also occur after a question, e.g.

ⲛⲓⲙ ⲡⲉⲧⲁϥⲛⲁⲩ ⲉⲣⲟϥ ⲧⲁⲣⲉϥⲥⲁϫⲓ ⲉⲣⲟϥ?
Who has seen him so as to be able to describe him?

If the question is rhetorical, as in this example, negation is generally implied: "No one has seen him so as…." If the question is real, the implication is "Tell me the answer so that…," as in

ⲉϥⲑⲱⲛ ⲡⲉⲕⲥⲟⲛ ⲧⲁⲣⲛ̄ⲥⲁϫⲓ ⲛⲉⲙⲁϥ?
Where is your brother that we may speak with him?

30.3 The Clause Conjugations. A distinction is made between sentence conjugations (Bipartite and Tripartite) and clause conjugations. The latter are so named because they correspond to a conjunction plus a clause in normal translation. To this category belong the Temporal, the Conjunctive, the Conditional, the Future Conjunctive of Result, and most uses of the Inflected Infinitive (ⲉⲧⲣⲉϥⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ, ϧⲉⲛ ⲡⲧⲣⲉϥⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ, ⲙⲉⲛⲉⲛⲥⲁ ⲧⲣⲉϥⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ). Characteristic of this category is (1) negation with -ϣⲧⲉⲙ-, and (2) the use of the Infinitive only.

A further clause conjugation is ϣⲁⲛⲧⲉϥⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ (until he hears):

ϣⲁⲛϯⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ until I hear ϣⲁⲛⲧⲉⲛⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
ϣⲁⲛⲧⲉⲕⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ until you hear ϣⲁⲛⲧⲉⲧⲉⲛⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
ϣⲁⲛⲧⲉⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ etc.
ϣⲁⲛⲧⲉϥⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ϣⲁⲛⲧⲟⲩⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
ϣⲁⲛⲧⲉⲥⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
ϣⲁⲛⲧⲉ-ⲡⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ until the man hears

Translation is regularly with "until," e.g.

ⲧⲉⲛⲛⲁϭⲱ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲁⲓⲙⲁ ϣⲁⲛⲧⲉϥⲓ. We shall remain here until he comes.

Similar in appearance to a clause conjugation is the form ϫⲓⲛ(ⲛ̀)ⲧⲁϥⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ (from the time that he heard). This consists, however, of the conjunction ϫⲓⲛ followed by the Second Perfect. Even more frequent are the compound expressions with ⲕⲁⲧⲁ ⲡⲣⲏϯ and ⲙ̀ ⲡⲣⲏϯ (as, according as, just as), both of which are followed by relative constructions, e.g.

ⲁⲩϩⲉⲓ ⲉⲣⲟϥ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲣⲏϯ ⲛ̄ⲧⲁϥϫⲟⲥ ⲛⲱⲟⲩ. They found it just as he had told them.
ⲕⲁⲧⲁ ⲡⲣⲏϯ ⲉⲧⲁⲓⲁⲓⲥ ⲛⲱⲧⲉⲛ, ⲉⲧⲉⲧⲛⲉⲁⲓⲥ ϩⲱⲧ-ⲑⲏⲛⲟⲩ… According as I have done to you, you too are to do…
ⲕⲁⲧⲁ ⲡⲣⲏϯ ⲉⲧ ⲥϧⲏⲟⲩⲧ ⲉⲑⲃⲏⲧϥ as it is written concerning him
ⲕⲁⲧⲁ ⲡⲣⲏϯ ⲉⲧⲟⲩⲛⲁϣⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲙ̀ⲙⲟⲥ according as they would be able to hear (i.e. understand)

The feminine resumptive -ⲥ in these constructions refers back to ⲡⲣⲏϯ and should not be translated as a pronominal object. If a real pronominal object is required, the resumptive -ⲥ is omitted, e.g.

ⲕⲁⲧⲁ ⲡⲣⲏϯ ⲛ̄ⲧⲁ-ⲡⲁⲓⲱⲧ ⲧⲛ̄ⲛⲟⲟⲩⲧ, ⲁⲛⲟⲕ ϩⲱ ϯϫⲉⲩ ⲙ̀ⲙⲱⲧⲉⲛ.
Just as my Father sent me, so I too am sending you.

Other constructions with ⲑⲉ are treated similarly, e.g.

ⲫⲁⲓ ⲡⲉ ⲡⲣⲏϯ ⲛ̄ⲧⲁ-ⲡϭⲟⲓⲥ ⲁⲓⲥ ⲛⲏⲓ.
Thus has the Lord acted for me.

30.4 When the Inflected Infinitive is used instead of a simple Infinitive after a verbal prefix, it has the value of a causative (hence its alternate name, the Causative Infinitive):

ⲁⲓⲧⲣⲉⲩⲓ ⲉϧⲟⲩⲛ. I caused them to enter.
ϯⲛⲁⲧⲣⲉⲕⲣⲓⲙⲓ. I shall cause you to weep.

30.5 The form ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲧⲉϥⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ describes an action as expected but not yet done. It is conveniently translated as "he has not yet heard". The form is fully inflected:

ⲙ̀ⲡⲁϯⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲧⲉⲛⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲧⲉ-ⲡⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲧⲉⲕⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲧⲉⲧⲉⲛⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲧⲉⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲧⲉϥⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲧⲟⲩⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ
ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲧⲉⲥⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ

It may occur in circumstantial clauses with the circumstantial converter ⲉ-; the resultant form appears ambiguously as ⲉ-ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲧⲉ- or simply ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲧⲉ-. In this usage it is best translated as an affirmative clause with "before":

ⲧⲉⲛⲛⲁⲧⲁϩⲟϥ ⲉ-ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲧⲉϥⲫⲟϩ ⲉ ⲧⲃⲁⲕⲓ.
We shall overtake him before he reaches the city.

With the imperfect converter ⲛⲉ-ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲧⲉϥⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ corresponds to the pluperfect: he had not yet heard.

30.6 An untranslatable dative with ⲛⲁ⸗ or ⲉⲣⲟ⸗ occurs optionally with many verbs, especially in the Imperative. This reflexive dative is called the ethical dative, following standard terminology. E.g.

ϣⲉ ⲛⲁⲕ ⲉ ⲡⲉⲕⲏⲓ. Go home!
ⲥⲱ ⲛⲱⲧⲉⲛ. Drink!

Verbs with which this occurs with some frequency are noted in the Glossary.

30.7 Higher numbers, ordinals, and fractions.

20 ϫⲱⲧ (f. ϫⲟⲩⲱⲧⲉ) ϫⲟⲩⲧ- 70 ϣϥⲉ, ⲥϣ̄ϥⲉ, ϣⲃⲉ
30 ⲙⲁⲡ (f. ⲙⲁⲁⲃⲉ) ⲙⲁⲡ- 80 ϧⲁⲙⲛⲉ, ϩⲙ̄ⲛⲉ-
40 ϩⲙⲉ 90 ⲡⲓⲥⲧⲁⲩ
50 ⲧⲁⲓⲟⲩ 100 ϣⲉ 200 ϣⲏⲧ
60 ⲥⲉ 1000 ϣⲟ 10,000 ⲑⲃⲁ

The tens combine with the forms of the units used in the 'teens (§24.3). The -ⲧ- of -ⲧⲏ (5) is not repeated after another -ⲧ-:

ϫⲟⲩⲧⲟⲩⲁⲓ 21 ⲙⲁⲡⲯⲓⲧ 39
ϫⲟⲩⲧϯⲟⲩ 25 ϣϥⲉϯⲟⲩ 75

An intrusive -ⲧ- appears before -ⲁϥⲧⲉ (4) and -ⲁⲥⲉ (6):

ⲙⲁⲡϥⲧⲱⲟⲩ 34 ⲥⲉⲥⲟⲟⲩ 66

The numbers ϣⲉ 100, ϣⲟ 1000, and ⲑⲃⲁ 10,000 are masculine:

ϣⲟ ⲥⲛⲁⲩ 2000 ⲙⲉⲧⲥⲛⲁⲩ ⲛ̀ ⲑⲃⲁ 120000
ϣⲟⲙⲧ ⲛ̀ ϣⲟ 3000

Proclitic forms of the units are frequent here, e.g.

ϣⲙ̄ⲧ-ϣⲟ 3000 ⲥⲉⲩ-ϣⲟ 6000

Combinations of these higher numbers with tens and units vary in form, e.g.

ϣⲉ ⲙⲁⲡ = ϣⲉ ⲛⲉⲙ ⲙⲁⲡ 130
ⲥⲉⲩ-ϣⲟ ⲟⲩⲟϩ ϣⲙⲏⲛ ⲛ̀ ϣⲉ 6800

Ordinal numbers are formed from the cardinals with the prefix ⲙⲁϩ-. The ordinals are treated as adjectives before the noun with linking ⲛ̀. Gender distinctions are maintained:

ⲡⲙⲁϩⲥⲛⲁⲩ ⲛ̀ ⲉϩⲟⲟⲩ the second day
ⲧⲙⲁϩⲥⲛⲟⲩϯ ⲛ̀ ⲣⲟⲙⲡⲓ the second year

For "first" the adjectives ϣⲟⲣⲡ (f. ϣⲟⲣⲡⲓ) and ϩⲟⲩⲓⲧ (f. ϩⲟⲩⲓϯ) are used.

Fractional numbers worth noting are ⲧ.ⲫⲁϣⲓ (half) and ϫⲟⲥ, ϫⲉⲥ- (half). Other fractions are expressed by ⲣⲉ- prefixed to the denominator, as in ⲣⲉ-ⲙⲏⲧ one-tenth, or with ⲟⲩⲱⲛ (ⲟⲩⲉⲛ-), as in ⲟⲩⲉⲛ-ⲛ̀-ϥⲧⲱⲟⲩ a fourth.

30.8 The remote (or further) demonstrative pronouns (that) are m.s. ⲫⲏ, f.s. ⲑⲏ, and pl. ⲛⲏ. These occur much less frequently than ⲫⲁⲓ, ⲑⲁⲓ, ⲛⲁⲓ because of the preference for using phrases with ⲉⲧ ⲙ̀ⲙⲁⲩ, such as ⲡⲉⲧ ⲙ̀ⲙⲁⲩ.

The prefixal forms ⲡⲓ-, ϯ-, and ⲛⲓ- are usually described as the reduced forms of ⲫⲏ, ⲑⲏ, and ⲛⲏ, parallel in usage to ⲡⲁⲓ-, ⲧⲁⲓ-, and ⲛⲁⲓ-. While such a formal relationship may exist, the use of ⲡⲓ-, ϯ-, and ⲛⲓ- in standard Sahidic is quite restricted. The form ⲡⲓ- occurs mainly in a few temporal and local adverbial expressions, such as ⲙ̀ ⲡⲓⲥⲏⲟⲩ (at that time) and ⲡⲓⲥⲁ (that side, as opposed to this side). The form ⲛⲓ- occurs most frequently in expressions involving comparison with ⲙ̀ ⲡⲣⲏϯ ⲛ̀ (like) or ⲉⲣ-ⲡⲣⲏϯ ⲛ̀ (to become like); it sometimes corresponds more closely to an English generic noun, e.g. ⲙ̀ ⲡⲣⲏϯ ⲛ̀ ⲛⲓϭⲣⲟⲙⲡⲓ like doves, like a dove. It is also found in the expression ϣⲁ ⲛⲓⲉⲛⲉϩ. Elsewhere ⲡⲓ-, ϯ-, and ⲛⲓ- are frequent as scribal variants of ⲡⲁⲓ-, ⲧⲁⲓ-, ⲛⲁⲓ- or have the force of an emphatic article.

30.9 When it is necessary to express a durative or continuous process or state in the future, a periphrastic construction is employed using the Circumstantial. Contrast

ⲕⲛⲁⲟⲩⲟⲡ you will become holy
ⲕⲛⲁϣⲱⲡⲓ ⲉⲕⲟⲩⲁⲃ you will be holy
ⲉⲕⲉⲭⲁ-ⲣⲱⲕ you shall become silent
ⲉⲕⲉϣⲱⲡⲓ ⲉⲕⲭⲱ ⲛ̀ ⲣⲱⲕ you shall remain silent

The difference is sometimes slight, but not infrequently spelled out. The same construction occasionally appears with other tripartite conjugational forms. A full discussion of the aspectual problem involved here lies beyond the scope of this book.

30.10 Greek conjunctions, adverbs, and prepositions that occur frequently in Coptic (for reference only). The term postpositive means that the word in question must follow immediately after the first element of the sentence, as in ⲡⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲇⲉ ⲁϥϣⲉ ⲛⲁϥ.

  • ⲁⲗⲗⲁ ἀλλά but, rather.
  • ⲁⲣⲁ ἄρα (introduces question).
  • ⲅⲁⲣ γάρ for, because, since (postpositive).
  • ⲇⲉ δέ but, however (postpositive).
  • ⲉⲓⲙⲏⲧⲓ εἰ μή τι (1) if not, unless, except that (+ Conj.); (2) elliptically, e.g. ⲙ̀ⲡⲟⲩϫⲉⲩ-ϩⲏⲗⲓⲁⲥ ϣⲁ ϩⲗⲓ ⲙ̀ⲙⲱⲟⲩ ⲉⲓⲙⲏⲧⲓ ⲉ ⲥⲁⲣⲉⲡⲧⲁ Elias was not sent to any of them except Sarepta. Note the independent pronoun in this usage: ⲙⲙⲟⲛ ϩⲗⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲣⲱⲙⲓ ⲛⲁⲉⲙⲓ ⲉⲣⲟϥ ⲉⲓⲙⲏⲧⲓ ⲁⲛⲟⲕ No one will understand it but me.
  • ⲉⲓⲧⲉ…ⲉⲓⲧⲉ εἴτε…εἴτε either … or.
  • ⲉⲡⲉⲓ ἐπεί because, since.
  • ⲉⲡⲉⲓⲇⲏ ἐπειδή because, since, when.
  • ⲉⲡⲉⲓⲇⲏⲡⲉⲣ ἐπειδήπερ inasmuch as, since.
  • ⲉⲧⲓ ἔτι yet, still, while yet (+ Circum.).
  • ⲏ ἤ or.
  • ⲕⲁⲓ ⲅⲁⲣ καὶ γάρ for truly.
  • ⲕⲁⲓⲧⲟⲓ καίτοι although, albeit.
  • ⲕⲁⲛ κἄν even if.
  • ⲕⲁⲧⲁ κατά (prep.) in accordance with, according to; also in distributive sense, e.g. ⲕⲁⲧⲁ ⲥⲁⲃⲃⲁⲧⲟⲛ every sabbath. Note the absence of the article here.
  • ⲙⲉⲛ…ⲇⲉ μέν…δέ balances two statements: on the one hand … but on the other. Both postpositive.
  • ⲙⲏ μή introduces a rhetorical question presuming a simple yes or no answer.
  • ⲙⲏⲡⲟⲧⲉ μήποτε so that not, lest (+ Conj.).
  • ⲙⲏⲡⲱⲥ μήπως so that not, lest (+ Conj.).
  • ⲙⲏⲧⲓ μήτι like ⲙⲏ, but with strong element of surprise.
  • ⲙⲟⲅⲓⲥ μόγις hardly, scarcely.
  • ⲟⲩⲛ οὖν therefore (postpositive).
  • ⲟⲩⲇⲉ οὐδέ and not, nor; the negation is often repeated in Coptic as well.
  • ⲟⲩⲧⲉ…ⲟⲩⲧⲉ οὔτε…οὔτε neither…nor.
  • ⲡⲣⲟⲥ πρός (prep.) used like ⲕⲁⲧⲁ.
  • ⲡⲱⲥ πῶς how? why?
  • ⲧⲟⲧⲉ τότε then, thereupon, next.
  • ϩⲟⲇⲁⲛ ὅταν when, whenever, if (+ Cond.).
  • ϩⲟⲥⲟⲛ, ⲛ̀ϩⲟⲥⲟⲛ ὅσον as long as (+ Circum.).
  • ϩⲱⲥ ὡς (1) as if; (2) although; (3) when, while as (all + Circum.).
  • ϩⲱⲥⲧⲉ ὥστε so that (+ Conj. or Infl. Inf.).
  • ⲭⲱⲣⲓⲥ χωρίς (prep.) without; a following noun has no indefinite article.

30.11 Final remarks on Coptic conjunctions and particles.

  1. The main coordinating conjunctions are ⲟⲩⲟϩ and ⲛⲉⲙ. ⲛⲉⲙ is used primarily to join nouns or nominalized expressions; ⲟⲩⲟϩ is used elsewhere. ⲟⲩⲟϩ is sometimes used for ⲛⲉⲙ, but this poses no particular translation problem. ⲟⲩⲟϩ often appears redundantly before the Conjunctive or before the apodosis of a conditional sentence. When nouns have no article (for whatever reason), they may be joined with the preposition ϩⲓ instead of ⲛⲉⲙ, as in ⲙⲙⲟⲛ ⲙⲱⲟⲩ ϩⲓ ⲱⲓⲕ ⲙ̀ⲙⲁⲩ There is neither water nor food. ϩⲓ is also used to form compound nominal expressions of a special type, e.g. ⲥⲁⲣⲝ ϩⲓ ⲥⲛⲟϥ flesh and blood. These expressions function as a unit: any article occurs only with the first word, as in ϩⲁⲛⲥⲁⲣⲝ ϩⲓ ⲥⲛⲟϥ ⲛⲉ They are flesh and blood.
  2. The main uses of the conjunction ϫⲉ have already been introduced: (1) in naming-constructions (see Vocab. 17); (2) to introduce noun clauses (object clauses) after appropriate verbs of speaking, perception, and the like; (3) to introduce purpose/result clauses with the Second or Third Future. ϫⲉ is also frequent in the sense "for, since, because", which is less ambiguously expressed by ⲉⲃⲟⲗ ϫⲉ and ⲉⲑⲃⲉ ϫⲉ. In many instances ϫⲉ is the equivalent of English "namely, i.e." in introducing explanatory appositions, e.g. ⲟⲩⲑⲩⲥⲓⲁ…ϫⲉ ⲟⲩⲥⲟⲉⲓϣ ⲛ̀ ϭⲣⲙ̄ⲡϣⲁⲛ an offering… namely a pair of turtle-doves. ϫⲉ is also used in some compound conjunctions, such as ⲛ̀ⲥⲁⲃⲏⲗ ϫⲉ (if not, unless) and ⲙ̀ ⲡⲣⲏϯ ϫⲉ (as if, as though).
  3. ⲓⲥϫⲉ and ⲓⲉ, in addition to their role in conditional sentences, may be placed before any statement to mark it as a question.
  4. ϭⲉ is a postpositive particle with very much the same function as Greek ⲇⲉ. It is especially frequent in the phrase ϯⲛⲟⲩ ϭⲉ and now, so now therefore.
  5. ⲛ̄ⲧⲟⲟⲩⲛ: then, thereupon, next, forthwith.

  6. ⲛ̀ⲥⲁ may mean "except" after a negative statement:

    ⲙ̀ⲡⲉ-ϩⲗⲓ ⲙ̀ⲙⲱⲟⲩ ⲧⲟⲩⲃⲟ ⲛ̀ⲥⲁ ⲛⲁⲓⲙⲁⲛ ⲡⲥⲩⲣⲟⲥ. None of them became cleansed except Naiman the Syrian.

  7. Certain temporal expressions may occur with a following relative clause without resumptive pronouns. These function virtually as compound conjunctions. E.g.

    ⲡⲉϩⲟⲟⲩ ⲉⲧⲉⲣⲉ-ⲛⲁⲓ ⲛⲁϣⲱⲡⲓ the day when this will happen
    ϧⲉⲛ ⲡⲉϩⲟⲟⲩ ⲛ̄ⲧⲁϥϫⲟⲩϣⲧ on the day when he looked
  8. The Conditional is frequently used in a temporal sense: when, whenever.

Vocabulary 30

  • ⲧⲉⲗⲏⲗ vb. intr. to rejoice (over: ⲉϫⲉⲛ); n.m. joy.
  • ⲧⲁϣⲟ ⲧⲁϣⲉ- ⲧⲁϣⲟ⸗ vb. tr. to increase (ⲙ̀ⲙⲟ⸗); often prefixed to another Inf.: to do something more, much. ⲧⲁϣⲉ-ⲟⲉⲓϣ to preach, proclaim (ⲙ̀ⲙⲟ⸗).
  • ⲧⲟⲩⲃⲟ ⲧⲟⲩⲃⲉ- ⲧⲟⲩⲃⲟ⸗ Q ⲧⲟⲩⲃⲏⲟⲩⲧ vb. tr. to purify, cleanse, heal (ⲙ̀ⲙⲟ⸗; of, from: ⲉ, ⲉⲃⲟⲗ ϧⲉⲛ, ϧⲁ); as n.m. purity, purification.
  • ⲧⲁⲩⲟ ⲧⲁⲟⲩⲉ- ⲧⲁⲟⲩⲟ⸗ (± ⲉⲃⲟⲗ) vb. tr. to send forth, cast forth, proclaim, tell (ⲙ̀ⲙⲟ⸗). ⲧⲁⲟⲩⲉ-ⲕⲁⲣⲡⲟⲥ to produce fruit.
  • ⲧⲁⲓⲟ ⲧⲁⲓⲉ- ⲧⲁⲓⲟ⸗ Q ⲧⲁⲓⲏⲟⲩⲧ vb. tr. to honor, respect. value, esteem (ⲙ̀ⲙⲟ⸗); Q to be honored etc., valuable.
  • ⲧⲁϫⲣⲟ ⲧⲁϫⲣⲉ- ⲧⲁϫⲣⲟ⸗ Q ⲧⲁϫⲣⲏⲟⲩⲧ vb. tr. to strengthen, confirm (ⲙ̀ⲙⲟ⸗); intr. to become strengthened, firm, resolute.
  • ⲡ.ⲥⲟⲡ time, occasion. ⲛ̄ ⲟⲩⲥⲟⲡ once. ϩⲓ ⲟⲩⲥⲟⲡ all at once, altogether. ⲛ̀ ⲕⲉⲥⲟⲡ again. ⲥⲟⲡ ⲛⲓⲃⲉⲛ always, on every occasion. ⲙ̀ ⲙⲏϣ ⲛ̀ ⲥⲟⲡ many times, often. ⲕⲁⲧⲁ ⲥⲟⲡ ⲛ̀ (+ Inf.) on every occasion of.
  • ⲡ.ϩⲱⲟⲩⲧ male (of animals or humans); freq. as adj.: male, wild, savage. ⲥϩⲓⲙⲓ is used as the corresponding female.
  • ⲡ.ⲭⲗⲟⲙ crown, wreath. ϯ-ⲭⲗⲟⲙ ⲉϫⲉⲛ to crown. ϭⲓ-ⲭⲗⲟⲙ to receive a crown, become a martyr.
  • ⲧ.ϧⲏⲓⲃⲓ shade, shadow. ⲉⲣ-ϧⲏⲓⲃⲓ to shade, protect (ⲉ, ⲉϫⲉⲛ).
  • ⲡ.ⲥⲉⲡⲓ remainder, rest (often in plural sense). A redundant -ⲕⲉ appears frequently: ⲡⲕⲉⲥⲉⲡⲓ the rest.
  • ⲉⲣ-ⲭⲣⲓⲁ to need (ⲙ̀ⲙⲟ⸗); to have to (do: ⲉ + Inf.); ⲭⲣⲓⲁ is Gk. ἡ χρεία.
  • ϫⲉⲙ-ⲡϣⲓⲛⲓ ⲛ̀, ϫⲉⲙ-ⲡ(⸗)ϣⲓⲛⲓ to search out, visit.
  • ϩⲣⲏⲓ is often used to reinforce a following preposition, esp. ϧⲉⲛ, with no real difference in sense.

Exercises

    • ⲡⲉϫⲁϥ ϫⲉ ⲙⲁⲣⲟⲛ, ϯⲟⲩⲛⲟⲩ ϧⲉⲛⲧ ⲉϧⲟⲩⲛ.
    • He said, "Let's go, the hour is at hand."
    • ⲁϥⲧⲣⲉ-ⲡⲉϥⲃⲱⲕ ⲑⲁⲙⲓⲟ ⲛⲁϥ ⲛ̀ ⲟⲩⲕⲟⲩϫⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲱⲓⲕ.
    • He caused his slave to prepare him a little bread.
    • ⲁϥⲧⲁϣⲉ-ⲟⲉⲓϣ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲉⲩⲁⲅⲅⲉⲗⲓⲟⲛ ϧⲉⲛ ⲧⲭⲱⲣⲁ ⲧⲏⲣⲥ ϣⲁⲛⲧⲉϥⲥⲁϩⲱϥ ⲉⲃⲟⲗ ⲛ̀ϧⲏⲧⲥ.
    • He proclaimed the gospel in the whole region until he withdrew from it.
    • ⲙ̀ⲡⲉⲣⲧⲣⲉ-ⲛϩⲁⲗⲁϯ ⲟⲩⲱⲙ ⲉⲃⲟⲗ ϧⲉⲛ ⲛⲁⲓⲁⲗⲟⲗⲓ.
    • Don't let the birds eat any of these grapes.
    • ⲁ-ⲛⲁⲓ ⲧⲏⲣⲟⲩ ϣⲱⲡⲓ ⲕⲁⲧⲁ ⲡⲣⲏϯ ⲉⲧ ⲥϧⲏⲟⲩⲧ ϧⲉⲛ ⲡϫⲱⲙ.
    • All these things happened just as is written in the book.
    • ϩⲣⲏⲓ ϧⲉⲛ ⲧⲙⲁϩⲙⲉⲧⲥⲛⲁⲩ ⲛ̀ ⲣⲟⲙⲡⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲧⲉϥⲙⲉⲧⲟⲩⲣⲟ ⲁϥⲙⲟⲩ ⲛ̀ϫⲉ ⲡⲉⲛⲟⲩⲣⲟ.
    • In the twelfth year of his reign, our king died.
    • ⲁⲙⲱⲓⲛⲓ ϣⲁⲣⲟⲓ ⲧⲁⲣⲉⲧⲛ̄ϫⲓⲙⲓ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲙⲧⲟⲛ.
    • Come (pl.) to me and you will find rest.
    • ϩⲱϯ ⲉⲣⲟⲛ ⲉⲧⲣⲉⲛⲥⲁϫⲓ ⲛⲉⲙⲁϥ ⲉ-ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲧⲉ-ⲧⲉϥⲧⲁⲡⲣⲟ ⲑⲱⲙ ϧⲉⲛ ⲡⲙⲟⲩ.
    • It is necessary for us to speak with him before his mouth closes in death.
    • ⲙⲁⲣⲉ-ⲡϭⲟⲓⲥ ϣⲁⲛ-ϩⲑⲏϥ ⲉϫⲱⲕ ⲛ̀ⲧⲉϥⲧⲁⲗϭⲟⲕ.
    • Let the Lord have pity on you (ms. sg.) and heal you.
    • ϣⲁⲣⲉ-ⲟⲩϣϣⲏⲛ ⲉ-ⲛⲁⲛⲉϥ ⲧⲁⲟⲩⲉ-ⲕⲁⲣⲡⲟⲥ ⲉ-ⲛⲁⲛⲉϥ.
    • A good tree produces good fruit.
    • ϯⲛⲁⲱⲥⲕ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲁⲓⲙⲁ ϣⲁⲛⲧⲉϥⲕⲧⲟϥ.
    • I will tarry here until he returns.
    • ⲉⲑⲃⲉ ⲫⲁⲓ ⲧⲉⲧⲛⲁϭⲓ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲭⲗⲟⲙ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲱⲟⲩ ϧⲉⲛ ⲙⲫⲏⲟⲩⲓ.
    • Because of this, you (pl.) will receive the crown of glory in the heavens.
    • ⲛ̀ ⲥϣⲉ ⲁⲛ ⲉⲧⲣⲉⲕⲧⲣⲉ-ⲡⲉⲧ ϩⲓⲑⲟⲩⲱⲕ ϫⲱⲛⲧ.
    • It is not proper for you (ms. sg.) to make your neighbor angry.
    • ⲡⲕⲉⲥⲉⲡⲓ ⲇⲉ ⲁⲩⲁⲣⲭⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲣⲓⲙⲓ ϩⲓ ⲟⲩⲥⲟⲡ.
    • The rest began to weep all at once.
    • ⲁ-ⲡⲁⲡ︤ⲛ︦ⲁ︥ ⲧⲉⲗⲏⲗ ⲉϫⲉⲛ ⲫⲛⲟⲩϯ ⲡⲁⲥⲱⲧⲏⲣ.
    • My spirit rejoiced over God my savior.
    • ⲁ-ⲡⲉⲧ ϣⲱⲛⲓ ϫⲟⲥ ⲛⲁϥ ϫⲉ ⲡϭⲟⲓⲥ, ⲟⲩⲟⲛ ϫⲟⲙ ⲙ̀ⲙⲟⲕ ⲉ ⲧⲟⲩⲃⲟⲓ.
    • The sick man said to him, "My lord, it is possible for you (ms. sg.) to heal me."
    • ⲛ̄ⲛⲉⲧⲛ̄ⲧⲁⲟⲩⲉ-ⲛⲉⲧⲁⲧⲉⲧⲉⲛⲛⲁⲩ ⲉⲣⲱⲟⲩ ⲉ ϩⲗⲓ.
    • You (pl.) shall not tell the things which you have seen to anyone.
    • ⲛϩⲁⲗⲁϯ ⲛ̀ ⲧⲫⲉ ϣⲁⲩⲟⲩⲱϩ ϧⲁ ⲧϧⲏⲓⲃⲓ ⲙ̀ ⲡϣϣⲏⲛ ⲉⲧ ⲙ̀ⲙⲁⲩ.
    • The birds of the sky settle under the shade of that tree.

    • Let the one who has two tunics give one to the one who does not have (any).
    • ⲧⲉⲛⲥⲱⲟⲩⲛ ϫⲉ ⲡϭⲟⲓⲥ ⲛⲁϫⲓⲙⲓ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲉⲛϣⲓⲛⲓ ⲛ̀ ⲕⲉⲥⲟⲡ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲉϩⲟⲟⲩ ⲉⲧ ⲙ̀ⲙⲁⲩ.
    • We know that the Lord will visit us again on that day.
    • ⲙ̀ⲡⲉⲛⲓⲣⲓ ⲕⲁⲧⲁ ⲡⲣⲏϯ ⲉⲧⲁϥϩⲱⲛ ⲉⲧⲟⲧⲛ ⲉ ⲁⲓⲥ.
    • We did not do as he commanded us to do.
    • ⲁϥⲧⲣⲉ-ⲡⲕⲉⲥⲉⲡⲓ ϩⲉⲙⲥⲓ ϫⲉⲕⲁⲥ ⲉⲩⲉⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲉ ⲧⲉϥⲥⲃⲱ.
    • He caused the rest to sit down so that they might hear his teaching.
    • ϥⲛⲁϯ-ⲭⲗⲟⲙ ⲉϫⲉⲛ ⲛⲉⲧ ⲛⲁⲉⲣ-ⲙⲉⲑⲣⲉ ⲉⲑⲃⲉ ⲡⲉϥⲣⲁⲛ ⲉⲧ ⲟⲩⲁⲃ.
    • He will crown the ones who will testify about his holy name.
    • ⲧϫⲟⲙ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲉⲧ ϭⲟⲥⲓ ⲧⲉⲧ ⲛⲁⲉⲣ-ϧⲏⲓⲃⲓ ⲉⲣⲟ.
    • It is the power of the Almighty which will protect you (fm. sg.).
    • ⲥⲱⲧⲉⲙ ⲉ ⲛⲁⲥⲁϫⲓ ⲧⲁⲣⲉⲕⲧⲁϫⲣⲟ ϧⲉⲛ ⲧⲡⲓⲥⲧⲓⲥ ϧⲉⲛ ⲟⲩⲱⲣϫ̄.
    • Listen to my words so that you (ms. sg.) will become strengthened firmly in the faith.
    • ⲁ-ⲡϭⲟⲓⲥ ⲧⲁϣⲉ-ⲡⲉϥⲛⲁⲓ ⲛⲉⲙⲁⲥ.
    • The Lord increased his mercy with her.
    • ⲟⲩϩⲱⲟⲩⲧ ⲛⲉⲙ ⲟⲩⲥϩⲓⲙⲓ ⲁϥⲑⲁⲙⲓⲟⲟⲩ ⲛ̀ϫⲉ ⲡϭⲟⲓⲥ.
    • Male and female, the Lord created them.
    • ⲛ̄ⲧⲁϥⲓ ⲉ ⲧⲟⲩⲃⲟⲟⲩ ⲉⲃⲟⲗ ϧⲉⲛ ⲛⲟⲩⲛⲟⲃⲓ.
    • It was to cleanse them from their sins that he came.
    • ⲙⲁⲣⲉⲛⲣⲁϣⲓ ⲛ̀ⲧⲉⲛⲧⲉⲗⲏⲗ ⲛ̀ⲧⲉⲛϯ-ⲱⲟⲩ ⲛⲁϥ.
    • Let us rejoice and be glad and praise him.
    • ⲛ̀ⲧⲉⲛⲉⲣ-ⲭⲣⲓⲁ ⲁⲛ ⲛ̀ ⲛⲉⲕⲥⲁϫⲓ ⲉⲧ ⲧⲁⲓⲏⲟⲩⲧ.
    • We do not need your (ms. sg.) respected words.

    • He had some male slaves and some female slaves.

    • It is possible for God to increase every grace.
    • ⲫⲁⲓ ⲡⲉ ⲡⲣⲁⲛ ⲉⲧⲁ-ⲡⲁⲅⲅⲉⲗⲟⲥ ⲧⲏⲓϥ ⲛⲁϥ ⲉ-ⲙ̀ⲡⲁⲧⲉ-ⲧⲉϥⲙⲁⲩ ⲃⲟⲕⲓ ⲙ̀ⲙⲟϥ ϧⲉⲛ ⲧⲛⲉϫⲓ.
    • This is the name which the angel gave him before his mother conceived him in the womb.

    • This cloak is more valuable than that (one).

    • She was a widow until she was eighty-four years old.

    • They say, "We will receive a crown in the heavens because of these great afflictions."

The Lord's Prayer

    • ⲡⲉⲛⲓⲱⲧ ⲉⲧ ϧⲉⲛ ⲙⲫⲏⲟⲩⲓ, ⲙⲁⲣⲉ-ⲡⲉⲕⲣⲁⲛ ⲟⲩⲟⲡ. ⲧⲉⲕⲙⲉⲧⲟⲩⲣⲟ ⲙⲁⲣⲉⲥⲓ. ⲡⲉⲕⲟⲩⲱϣ ⲙⲁⲣⲉϥϣⲱⲡⲓ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲣⲏϯ ⲉⲧⲉϥϧⲉⲛ ⲧⲫⲉ ⲛ̀ⲧⲉϥϣⲱⲡⲓ1 ⲟⲛ ϩⲓϫⲉⲛ ⲡⲕⲁϩⲓ. ⲡⲉⲛⲱⲓⲕ ⲉⲧ ⲛⲏⲟⲩ2 ⲛ̀ⲧⲉⲕϯ ⲙ̀ⲙⲟϥ ⲛⲁⲛ ⲙ̀ ⲫⲟⲟⲩ, ⲛ̀ⲧⲉⲕⲭⲱ ⲛⲁⲛ ⲉⲃⲟⲗ ⲛ̀ ⲛⲉⲧ ⲉⲣⲟⲛ3 ⲙ̀ ⲡⲣⲏϯ ϩⲱⲛ ⲟⲛ ⲉⲧⲉⲛⲭⲱ ⲉⲃⲟⲗ ⲛ̀ ⲛⲉⲧⲉ ⲟⲩⲟⲛⲧⲁⲛ ⲉⲣⲱⲟⲩ, ⲛ̀ⲧⲉⲕϣⲧⲉⲙϭⲓⲧⲛ ⲉϧⲟⲩⲛ ⲉ ⲡⲉⲓⲣⲁⲥⲙⲟⲥ ⲁⲗⲗⲁ ⲛ̀ⲧⲉⲕⲛⲁϩⲙⲛ4 ⲉⲃⲟⲗ ϩⲓⲧⲟⲧϥ ⲙ̀ ⲡⲡⲟⲛⲏⲣⲟⲥ, ϫⲉ ⲧⲱⲕ ⲧⲉ ⲧϫⲟⲙ ⲛⲉⲙ ⲡⲱⲟⲩ ϣⲁ ⲛⲓⲉⲛⲉϩ. ⲁⲙⲏⲛ.
    • Our father who is in the heavens, may your name be hallowed. May your kingdom come. May your will happen as in heaven and happen also on the earth. Our bread which is coming, give to us today, and forgive us the things which are due from us, just as we ourselves also forgive the ones from whom we have things due, and do not take us into temptation, but save us from evil, for yours is the power and the glory forever. Amen.
  1. The repetition of the verb is apparently an attempt to clarify what was felt as an awkward construction in the Greek.
  2. ⲉⲧ ⲛⲏⲟⲩ renders Gk. ἐπιούσιον "for the coming (day)." Note that the 2nd pers. Conjunctives continue, with the force of Imperatives, the 3rd pers. Injunctive forms at the beginning.
  3. The prep. ⲉ has the special sense of "due from (as indebtedness)". Thus, ⲛⲉⲧ ⲉⲣⲟⲛ "those things which are due from us," ⲛⲉⲧⲉ ⲟⲩⲟⲛⲧⲁⲛ ⲉⲣⲱⲟⲩ "those from whom we have (something) due."
  4. ⲛⲟϩⲉⲙ vb. tr. to rescue, save.
